Then, several matters concerning the recruitment of donations were discussed, and the meeting adjourned at 4:50 PM.

Flood Relief Association; Promoting the Sale of Soy Sauce to Contribute to Relief; Many People Have Been Enthusiastically Buying Goods in Recent Days 108

The Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Flood Relief Association of Various Provinces believes that the floods in various places this year are severe, exceeding those of the past. Moreover, winter is approaching, with howling north winds, and people are suffering from hunger and cold. If they do not starve to death, they will freeze to death. Therefore, this relief work cannot be delayed for even a moment. The Flood Relief Association, on behalf of the disaster victims, has appealed to all parties for donations and has held various activities to use all the income for relief. Since the start of fundraising, it has gained the sympathy of all walks of life and has received enthusiastic donations, resulting in significant results. The recent total mobilization of the Boy Scouts for fundraising is a clear example. The Chinese Agricultural Chemical Manufacturing Factory, which has been established in this city for many years, aims to promote rural products and consolidate the rural economy. Currently, its product is a type of "Three Fresh" soy sauce, which is manufactured using scientific principles and absolutely avoids oleic acid preservatives. The factory, in view of the severity of this year's disaster, is willing to sell 30,000 bottles of this soy sauce and contribute the proceeds to relief in order to save the disaster-stricken people. This measure has been implemented for many days. In addition to requesting the Boy Scouts to help with sales, the Flood Relief Association has sent letters to all sectors, requesting them to recognize and sell the soy sauce. Because soy sauce is a necessity for households, and the money is not wasted, this can both help the disaster victims and be practical. According to Mr. Shen of the factory, many people have been enthusiastically picking up the goods in recent days. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will purchase them as soon as possible to avoid missing out.

News from the Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association; The Number of Participants in Chain Relief is Increasing Daily 109

The Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association on Renji Road was reorganized in the Republic of China year 9 (1920) due to the severe drought in the five northern provinces and became a permanent charitable organization in Shanghai. It has achieved considerable success in relief and disaster prevention. It does not issue donation books to avoid abuse. Over the past decades, it has been trusted both at home and abroad. The donations directly sent to the association amount to no less than tens of millions. Each time relief is distributed, personnel are dispatched to supervise the distribution together with local Chinese and Western gentlemen. This summer, the rivers have once again experienced massive flooding, following a severe drought in the southeast. Moreover, the disaster area is spreading wider and wider. Relief efforts are now underway in provinces such as Jiangsu, Shandong, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Fujian, and Guangdong, and relief funds and clothing amounting to more than 270,000 yuan have been allocated. However, the market is sluggish, and donations are extremely difficult. Chain relief has been repeatedly promoted by all sectors to gather strength and save the people suffering from the flood. Since the association complied with this, it has been praised by Chinese and foreign legal experts in Shanghai as a very legitimate method. Not only are there many sponsors, but the number of participants is also increasing daily, with monthly relief funds exceeding 1,000 yuan, and possibly doubling each month. During this tense period, it is truly a good strategy for raising relief funds. During the developmental stage, some who do not understand the content have pointed out that it is akin to gambling. However, they do not know that this method stipulates that each person donates 30 cents, of which 20 cents is for disaster relief, and 10 cents is for the chain. The rewards for those listed first in the letter are mostly not accepted but are entirely transferred to relief funds. Even those who are willing to enjoy the benefits will either use them for public welfare or help other charitable causes. There is no competitive nature. The so-called waste is small, and the preservation is great. The association has received frequent telephone calls in recent days. The matter concerns joint disaster relief, and it is hoped that all sectors will not interrupt it due to one statement, which will affect the disaster victims waiting to be fed.

Rent Reduction Movement in the Concessions 112

Rongren Lane and Yuelaifang

Tenants of Rongren Lane and Yuelaifang on Xujiahui Road and Caishi Road in the French Concession felt that the market was sluggish and business was in decline. Rent reduction was necessary for prosperity. Therefore, they held an inaugural meeting in the lane the other day. Chen Jiufeng of the Municipal Rent Reduction Committee attended to provide guidance. Officer Hua of the Political Department of the French Concession Police monitored the meeting. Li Zhuxi, Chen Jueting, Huang Zhenming, Liu Jialin, Li Shoubai, and other five people were elected as the presidium to report on the progress of the initiative. More than half of the tenants have joined, so a formal establishment was held. The following resolutions were discussed and decided: (1) To determine the standard for rent reduction. According to the precedent of the Municipal Rent Reduction Association, rent will be paid at 60%, but the minimum limit is now set at 80%. (2) When should the rent reduction begin? It should start from September. In addition, the three months of rent owed during the Shanghai War should also be waived by the landlord. (3) How should the drinking water problem be solved? The well water used in the past was paid for within the rent. The landlords are trying to make extra profits and changed to salty well water without notice. Therefore, it was decided to restore the original state. (4) What should be done if the landlord does not agree to the request? If there is no rent reduction and no change of water, then rent payment will be stopped. The rent will be temporarily deposited in the bank for safekeeping. The designated bank and procedures will be announced separately. (5) How should members be protected? The association will hire a lawyer as a legal consultant. (6) How should litigation expenses be raised? It is generally recognized by each . After the above resolutions were passed by the entire body, they were submitted to higher authorities . In addition to the case, a letter was sent to the landlord, and the meeting was adjourned.

Fulan Road

Tao Peng Road and Lan Road , Ke Fanweide, Wang Fu , and others, in view of the pressure of high rents, wanted to seek reductions to alleviate difficulties. They united Xinlao Weixing Lane, and all tenants joined the Shanghai Municipal All-Tenant Rent Reduction Federation to organize the Fourth Branch. An inaugural meeting was held yesterday. More than 200 tenants attended. Zhuo Wen, Chen Zhixiong, and Li Zhengfang were sent by the Federation to provide guidance. Fan Weide was elected as the temporary chairman, and Li Hetang was the recorder. The meeting was held with due respect. Jing Xinkesheng, Chen Jinhuai, Li Hetang, Lin Cisheng, Su Zhifang, Fan Weide, Huang Xiangkang, Wu Canpeng, Li Jutong, Jin Shuhe, Li Zenggui, Wang Fuyou, Wang Gaofeng, Wang Yisheng, Pan Shaoliang, Jiang Hongru, Ding Yunfei, and other seventeen people were elected as executive committee members. It was resolved and passed that: (1) The major landlord should be requested to reduce the rent in Xinlao Weixing Lane by 60%. (2) The Federation should be requested to send letters to all tenants in the city for unanimous support. (3) If the rent is not reduced, the rent will not be paid and will be temporarily stored in the bank, pending resolution.

Deceased Female Professor Zhang Duanzhen's Inheritance Dispute 114

Zhang Duanzhen, a woman from Minhou, residing at No. 8 Changgning Lane, Jisi Feier Road, was deeply knowledgeable in literature and served as a professor at various universities. Unfortunately, she passed away on July 26th of this year after a sudden illness. Ms. Zhang's father (Zhang Zhuohou) passed away early in her childhood, and she had many siblings. Therefore, she strived to excel and studied diligently. Over the years, she accumulated savings, which, apart from generous donations to public welfare, were used to purchase stocks and government bonds, totaling over 10,000 yuan, deposited in the bank. After falling ill in Shanghai this time, she had already prepared a will on July 15th, stating that in case of any unforeseen events, all her inheritance would be managed entirely by her younger brother, Zhang Xifan. Xifan, who was studying in Shanghai, received the will of his deceased sister and, fearing opposition from others, engaged two lawyers, Yao Qiming and Cheng Xiuling, to file a lawsuit in the local court against his sisters, such as Zhang Meizhen, Lin Zhang Shuzhen, and Li Zhang Wanzhen, seeking confirmation of the will. After receiving the complaint, the court once summoned them for a hearing. However, Zhang Xifan did not appear due to illness, and the court ordered a new summons. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Pang Shurong specially opened the first court for the trial. The plaintiff, Zhang Xifan, accompanied by his engaged lawyers, Yao and Cheng, appeared in court. The defendants also engaged two lawyers, Chen Jinji and Da Jiaoxian, who subsequently arrived in court to present their defense. Zhang Xifan first recounted the previous events, followed by the testimony of witnesses Dong Zhao Yinxiang and He Zhang Lizhen, who described Zhang Duanzhen's illness in the hospital and the details of writing the will, which was very detailed. According to them, the wording of the will was based entirely on Duanzhen's dictation. Zhang Xifan further stated that he wished to use all the inheritance of his deceased sister for charitable causes, leaving a permanent memorial. When the judge questioned Zhang Meizhen and Zhang Wanzhen, they said that they also agreed to the transfer to charitable causes, but the issue of whether the will was forged should be resolved first. The judge said that they were siblings and should each make concessions, and then instructed the lawyers of both parties to conduct reconciliation outside the court before further adjudication.

Germany and the United States Restrict Trade in Military Supplies; Each Has Telegraphed Instructions to Their Shanghai Trading Houses; Transactions Not Allowed Without Government Permission 116

The German trading houses in this port, including Zenchchen, Siemens, Lihe, Kongshi, Huadelong, and Qianxin, along with over thirty other major trading houses, have recently received telegrams from their headquarters in Germany stating that, according to orders from the German government, the large-scale export of military-use metal materials and other items will be temporarily suspended from the 16th of this month. All orders for such transactions must not be rashly signed without first consulting the government for permission. Additionally, major American trading houses such as Shenchang and Maosheng have also received telegrams from their headquarters stating that, starting this month, they are no longer allowed to place large orders for military supplies such as steel plates and bars, and transactions can only be completed with the permission of the American government. The telegrams did not explicitly state how to handle future transactions or when free trade would be allowed. The American side estimates that the order will not be lifted until January of next year at the earliest. Recalling the similar restrictions before the outbreak of the European War in 1914, one can imagine the situation in Europe and the turbulence in the Far East.

Ancient Vase Lawsuit 117

Cheng Linsheng Must Appear in Court; Ancient Vase Temporarily Stored in Court

An ancient vase owned by real estate merchant Cheng Linsheng, named Guyuexuan and dating back to the Qianlong era, is now the subject of a lawsuit due to a mortgage dispute. Chi Yunfei from Fujian has engaged a lawyer to sue Jiang Yuting, the owner of Yuanzhang Jewelry Store at No. 99 Jiangxi Road, who is from Wuxi, for fraudulently obtaining the vase in the First Special District Court. The court has already summoned him and ordered him to bring Cheng Linsheng to court to testify and to bring the vase to court for further verification. This was reported in this newspaper on the 12th of this month. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao of the First Special Court opened the fifth criminal court for further hearings. Cheng Linsheng did not appear due to illness, and lawyer Hu Jue appeared in court as his representative. Judge Ye stated that Cheng himself must appear in court for this case and cannot be represented. If Cheng does not appear next time, the court may arrest him. When questioned, Jiang Yuting stated that Cheng owed him 18,000 yuan in bill payments and mortgaged the Guyuexuan vase and two diamond rings to him. Cheng later took the vase away for more than a week and exchanged it for the calligraphy "Myriad Countries Come to Court," and then switched it back. He has already sued Cheng in the Second Special District Court, and because Cheng raised the issue of jurisdiction, the case was transferred to this court. The vase has been submitted as evidence. The vase is only about three inches long and about one inch in circumference. The mouth of the vase has two ears and is painted with colorful beauties. It is stored in a rosewood box, and the bottom of the box has a Qianlong imperial inscription. The plaintiff pointed out that one of the ears of the vase has a slight yellow tint. After careful inspection, Judge Ye ordered that Cheng Linsheng be summoned to court again at a later date for further questioning. The ancient vase is temporarily stored in this court.

Dancer Huang Aizhen Sues for Offense Against Morality 118

Inducing Loss of Chastity, Cohabitation, and Abandonment; Dancer's Lawsuit Is Like This; Defendant Jiang Bifeng Is Absent

Huang Aizhen, a woman from Huzhou, is 28 years old, with a beautiful appearance, and works as a dancer in the New York Dance Hall on Zhubaoshan Road in the French Concession. In July of this year, while Huang was dancing at the Xiaoyao Dance Hall on Xizang Road, she was seduced and lost her chastity to a dance partner named Jiang Bifeng, who also swindled her out of her clothing and silver dollars. Therefore, recently, Huang's father, Huang Wenkui, acting as her legal guardian, engaged lawyer Hu Jue to file a lawsuit against Jiang Bifeng in the First Special District Court for offense against morality, requesting a summons and legal proceedings. It is noted that Huang Aizhen came to Shanghai from her hometown with her aunt, Ms. Feng, in the spring of this year to learn dancing skills in order to earn a living. In July and August, she entered the Xiaoyao Dance Hall on Xizang Road as a dancer. Because of her excellent appearance and skills, her career was flourishing, so she had some savings. Jiang Bifeng, seeing that Huang was young and beautiful, used seductive tactics. One evening, he falsely claimed to be hosting a banquet and led Huang to the Wugong Hotel on Fuzhou Road. Unexpectedly, upon entering the room, there was no one there. Huang wanted to leave, but Jiang refused, closing the door and raping her. At the time, Jiang claimed to be a shareholder in the Xiaoyao Dance Hall, wealthy, and unmarried, and firmly instructed Huang not to tell her parents about the rape. Later, he rented a house at No. 10 Chengqi Lane on Race Course Road and began cohabiting with her. However, less than two months later, their love suddenly ended. Recently, Jiang disappeared without a trace. Huang, feeling defiled and having been swindled out of 600 yuan in dance earnings and her clothing, was filled with anger and wanted to seek justice through the law. However, because Huang is only sixteen years old, she does not have the right to file a lawsuit independently under the law. Therefore, her father, Huang Wenkui, acted as her legal guardian and engaged a lawyer to file a lawsuit. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi presided over the third criminal court for the hearing. The defendant, Jiang Bifeng, was absent. Huang Aizhen stated that she currently lives at No. 4 Yikang Lane on Meibeger Road, with a fellow townsman. Her father, Huang Wenkui, was unable to attend court due to illness. Judge Jiang ordered that the case be rescheduled for next Monday afternoon.

Punishment for Retrieving Silver from Water 119

Police Prosecute for Embezzlement; Luo San Fined Fifteen Yuan

Since the Ministry of Finance implemented the legal tender policy, there have been many unscrupulous merchants who have taken the opportunity to buy silver dollars for outflow and profit. At 9:20 PM on the 10th of this month, Luo San, a man from Qingkou, suddenly heard the sound of something heavy being thrown into the Huangpu River at the Qinhuangdao Wharf in Yangshupu. He immediately went to investigate and managed to retrieve a hundred silver dollars wrapped in cloth. He intended to take them home, but he was intercepted by Hua Constable No. 3417, who questioned him about the situation and took him to the Huishan Police Station and then to the First Special District Local Court for temporary detention and investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiepan presided over the third criminal court hearing. Gongbuju lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that it was impossible to find the principal offender during the investigation and prosecuted the defendant for embezzlement under Article 337 of the Criminal Law, requesting his prosecution. The defendant claimed that he only heard the sound of water and did not see any person or trace. Judge Xiao ruled that Luo San was guilty of embezzling lost property and fined him fifteen yuan. If he could not pay the fine, he would be sentenced to labor at a rate of two yuan per day. The one hundred silver dollars were confiscated.

Lin Chenghuan, a man from Ningbo, 37 years old, lived at No. 4 Shikang Lane, 975 Zhejiang Road, and ran a cloth shop at No. 37 Ningbo Road. The Chinese Christian Independent Church Held a Third Anniversary Memorial Ceremony for Yu Zongzhou Yesterday 121

Yesterday, the National General Assembly of the Chinese Christian Independent Church held a third anniversary memorial ceremony for Mr. Yu Zongzhou. At the main entrance of the church on Xiangyin Road, a white cloth banner hung, reading "Third Anniversary Memorial of Mr. Yu Gong Zongzhou's Death," alongside the national flag of the Republic of China. The grand hall was filled with flowers, and a portrait of Mr. Yu was placed on the stage, creating a very solemn atmosphere. The meeting began promptly with the ringing of a bell to mark the mourning. Zhu Baoluo led the singing of hymns, Liu Yumei offered a prayer, Zhu Baoluo read scriptures, and then more hymns were sung. Wang Hong reported on the significance of the meeting, stating that thirty years ago, the Christian churches in our country were under the jurisdiction of Western missions, and everything was done according to the Western pastors. Chinese believers had no possibility of speaking out. However, Yu Gong Zongzhou, with the wisdom of a pioneer and the spirit of courage and perseverance, was able to form a completely Chinese Christian Independent Church. This not only opened a new era in Christianity in our country but also made a great contribution to the Chinese nation. His great achievements will be immortal. Religious affairs are essentially for the spiritual cultivation of individuals and should not be dominated by others. We used to be like newborns in our religious lives, relying on others for everything. Now that we have grown up, we should have autonomy and not blindly follow others. Yu Gong devoted himself to independence for more than thirty years. Today, Chinese churches have gradually achieved economic self-sufficiency and recovered the autonomy of church power. Looking back and looking forward, we should commemorate Mr. Yu's death every year. However, what is the significance of holding such a memorial meeting? Today, I will briefly present three points about Mr. Yu's achievements to encourage everyone: (1) Mr. Yu had a spirit of creation. One of the biggest problems of us Chinese people is that we like to imitate others in everything. We are so-called "fond of the new and tired of the old," "saying what others say," "running high and chasing the red," and "treading on the powerful." Seeing that others have some benefits, we rush to imitate them, resulting in both sides being injured, and we lack the spirit of creation and the ability to build. At that time, Mr. Yu's establishment of the Independent Church was something that others did not know and did not do. (2) Mr. Yu made friends and used people based on the principle of trust throughout his life, adhering to the principle of mutual trust and mutual establishment. He treated people with sincerity and had no suspicion or scruples. Therefore, later generations all have a positive evaluation of him. Mr. Yu did use some people improperly during his lifetime. However, we do not know that Mr. Yu had a righteous and upright mind, so he did not suspect others of having malicious intentions. He did not measure gentlemen with the hearts of petty people and adhered to the principle of "do not doubt people you use, and do not use people you doubt." This is an indispensable criterion for leaders. (3) Mr. Yu devoted his life to religious work for more than fifty years. His words and actions were completely consistent. Mr. Yu did so many great things that benefited society and relieved the suffering of individuals. Mr. Yu completely adhered to the principle of faith and practice, using faith as the warp and practice as the weft, and fully demonstrated the Christian spirit of love, sacrifice, and saving people, making everyone who heard and saw it feel convinced. Christianity has been introduced from the West for more than a hundred years, with more than 400,000 followers. Even from the establishment of this church to the present, it has been more than thirty years. However, it has not penetrated deeply into people's hearts because most people can talk but cannot act, so the work of the kingdom of heaven cannot be realized on earth, as it is in heaven. Glory belongs to the Lord. In the future, all our believers must bear this responsibility of practice, so that the original face of Christianity can be realized in the human world and make practical contributions to the country and the nation. This is the three-point significance of today's memorial meeting. After the report, the entire assembly stood up in silence for three minutes. Li Keyong led the recitation, Sun Delin reported on his life story, hymns were sung, and Reverend Lin Timothy preached. Then, You Lanjie and Hong Kunshan gave speeches, Mr. Yu's son, Zu Guang, delivered a speech, prayers were offered, and photographs were taken before the meeting adjourned. Each person was given a package of tea and snacks as a memorial.

Lonely Old Man Hangs Himself in Bed 127

Niece Sleeps with the Deceased for a Night Before Discovering It the Next Morning

Rui JiaChun, a 65-year-old from Nanjing, was a tinsmith. His wife had passed away early, and he had no children. He was an old man living alone and rented a bed in the home of Wang Dai Shi, the landlady, at No. 7 Rongyuan Lane, 225 Datong Road, Zhabei, for ten cents a month. In August, he moved to live with his cousin, Rui Chuandao, at No. 25 Jiqing Lane, Haichang Road, Zhabei. Recently, due to his old age and inability to work, his life had become exceptionally difficult, so he often went to his niece, Zhu Fengqin, at No. 12 Taiheng Lane, West Gate, Nanshi. Zhu, 22 years old, was a local and worked in a sock factory on Lin Yin Road for a living. Sometimes her uncle would come to visit and give her one or two yuan. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the day before yesterday, Rui Jiachun went to Fengqin's place again, but Fengqin was out. Later, the landlady, Lin Yangshi, received him. Rui Jiachun went to his niece's bedroom in the pavilion. At about 11 o'clock at night, Zhu Fengqin returned home and did not know that her uncle was inside, so she went to bed to sleep. At about 9 o'clock the next morning, Fengqin got up and went behind the bed to relieve herself. She found that her uncle, Rui Jiachun, was hanging high on the bed frame and had hanged himself. Fengqin was shocked and called the landlady to come and see. She also reported the matter to the local policeman, who then reported it to the West Gate Branch to file a case, stating the above situation. The branch then ordered the local guarantor to report to the court for an inquest. In the afternoon at 5 o'clock, the court sent a prosecutor to conduct an examination on the spot, confirming that he had hanged himself. In addition to filling out the death certificate, he ordered the relatives to prepare a coffin for burial.

Municipal Health Bureau Strictly Enforces Revised Hospital Registration Rules 129

Adding Minimum Standards for Hospital Establishment; Strictly Cracking Down on Those Lacking Adequate Equipment

The Municipal Health Bureau believes that the Ministry-promulgated Hospital Management Regulations lack clear provisions on hospital equipment standards, and the city's Hospital Registration Regulations do not specify the minimum requirements for hospital establishment. In order to facilitate management and rectification, the city's Academy Registration Regulations have been revised to include the minimum standards for hospital establishment, providing a basis for enforcement. The regulations have been approved by the municipal government and will be implemented immediately. The regulations are as follows: Article 1: All public and private hospitals in the city, except municipal hospitals, shall apply to the Municipal Health Bureau for registration in accordance with these regulations. No establishment shall be allowed without approval and registration certificate. Article 2: When applying for registration, hospitals shall comply with the following provisions in addition to the provisions of the Ministry-promulgated Management Regulations: (1) Formal physicians registered with the Municipal Health Bureau shall not serve as hospital directors; (2) Hospitals without special equipment for a particular department and deemed qualified by the Municipal Health Bureau shall not be called specialty hospitals; (3) Each hospital must have at least ten beds, with each bed occupying at least six square meters; (4) Hospitals must have intensive care rooms and morgue facilities. Article 3: When applying for registration, hospitals shall submit a completed application form, along with building plans and a license fee of four yuan and a stamp duty of one yuan to the Municipal Health Bureau. A license will be issued only after the application has been reviewed and approved. Article 4: Hospital registration licenses shall be renewed annually and the license fee and stamp duty shall be paid as specified in the previous article. A fee of one yuan shall be paid for license renewal due to relocation during the term, and stamp duty shall be affixed in accordance with regulations. Article 5: Each hospital shall hang its license in the registration area for public viewing. Article 6: If a license is lost, an application may be made for a replacement, but all fees shall be paid and a statement shall be published in the newspaper declaring the license invalid. Article 7: Violators of these regulations shall be punished in accordance with the Ministry-promulgated Hospital Management Regulations. Article 8: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any unaddressed matters. Article 9: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation. It is heard that the Municipal Health Bureau will strictly crack down on hospitals in the city with poor equipment and excessive publicity in accordance with the regulations in the future.

Further News on the Guangdong Miss's Maid Abuse Case 138

The Children's Welfare Association Commends Whistleblower Tan Guanman

According to Huadong News, the case of Guangdong Miss Tan Huishu, residing at 47 Deren Lane, Xingjia Mu Bridge, Zhabei, abusing her maid, which was exposed by a righteous person in September of this year, has been publicly prosecuted by Prosecutor Tang of the local court since October. Zhang, the judge, has held two court sessions and, based on the fact that the charges were substantiated, sentenced Tan Huishu to one year and six months of imprisonment. The reporter notes that in November of last year, Huabei also had the case of Tianjin Miss Chen Xiangjun abusing her maid. After the Tianjin Local Court's trial, Chen Xiangjun was found guilty of repeatedly injuring the victim and was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. Now, the Guangdong Miss Tan Huishu's maid abuse case is quite similar. The people are similar, the case is similar, and the punishment is similar. The reporter notes that this case was initially reported to the Public Security Bureau by the China Children's Welfare Association, which paid close attention to the progress of the case. According to the person in charge of the association, the reason why the association paid close attention to this case was entirely out of concern for the happiness of children and not out of any resentment towards Tan Huishu personally. Now that Miss Tan has been sentenced to imprisonment, it is hoped that through this lesson, she can reflect on her past actions and encourage herself in the future and never blame any individual. During the trial of this case, Patrol Officer Zuo Shaozeng of the Yongxing Road Police Station and Qi Baoqing, the gatekeeper of Deren Lane, all testified righteously without fear, which is truly admirable. As for Mr. Tan Guanman, a teacher at Qiming Elementary School, because of his reporting of this case, he was ambushed and injured by villains while walking on the road the other day. The association expresses its deep sympathy and, in addition to taking measures to assist in the arrest of the murderers, resolved at yesterday's meeting of directors to present Mr. Tan with a silver shield engraved with the words "Speak Righteously," as a memento to express its appreciation.

Continued Trial of Tang Akun's Murder Case 140

Suddenly, a Man Claiming to be Akun's Uncle Appeared and Asked the Court to Seek Justice for the Deceased

Tang Akun, a local resident of 491 Kangnaotuo Road, Shanghai West, once served as the captain of the anti-smoking investigation team in Changzhou. After being dismissed, he remained unemployed at home. At about 8:00 AM on November 16 of last year, Tang Akun and Yan Shengquan were walking near Yan's House when Tang was hacked to death with an axe. Afterwards, Tang's wife, Tang Ji, accused Yan Shengquan, a local resident of Yan's House, of conspiring with Zhao A'er and two others to murder her husband and requested justice. After receiving the accusation, the court repeatedly ordered the arrest of the perpetrators without success. Recently, Yan secretly returned to Shanghai and was arrested by the police and sent to the local court. Prosecutor Xie Lian investigated and confirmed the facts and prosecuted him in the criminal court for the crime of joint murder. Judge Wu Deying has held several trials without a conclusion. The details have been repeatedly recorded in previous newspapers. It is now learned that this case was again heard by Judge Wu at 2:00 PM yesterday. The plaintiff, Tang Ji, appeared in court and recounted the previous events and requested the return of 7,600 yuan in private compensation. Another plaintiff, Tang A'gen, then testified, stating that he was 55 years old, from Jiading, and made a living by farming. Tang Akun was his nephew. He had three brothers, all of whom have passed away. Akun was the son of his elder brother and recognized him as his father, which was known throughout the hometown. In recent years, because he was old and weak, the family expenses were entirely supported by Akun. Since Akun was murdered by Yan Shengquan last winter, his livelihood has been cut off. Moreover, he was the only son in the third generation. He learned from his fellow villager Zhao Xiaomao that the murderer had been arrested, so he requested justice and the return of more than 10,000 yuan in private compensation. The judge was very surprised by the testimony and asked Tang Ji, "Do you know Tang A'gen?" Tang Ji replied, "Tang Akun and I have been living together for five or six years. I have never heard of this uncle in the countryside." Tang A'gen said, "I often go to her place (referring to Tang Ji). She is my child Akun's concubine." Tang Ji lowered her head and remained silent upon hearing this. The judge ordered Zhao Xiaomao to testify. He was 26 years old, from Jiading. On November 5, he was drinking tea and reading the newspaper at the Siyang Tea House in Caojiadu, reading aloud that the murderers of Tang Akun had been arrested and detained. He was overheard by this old man (pointing to Tang A'gen), who claimed to be the uncle of the deceased and inquired about the details reported in the newspaper. Unexpectedly, two other tea customers at another table, Li Wencai and Zhang Suilin, joined the conversation. Li and Zhang both said, "We used to work with Tang Akun. Tang had a feud with Yan because of selling opium, so Tang Akun was actually murdered by Yan. Today, I was invited to court by Tang A'gen to testify." Yan Shengquan, who was in custody, testified that he was 36 years old. After Tang Akun was hacked to death, he went to other ports to work as a car driver. He has now returned to Shanghai due to unemployment. It is a false accusation to accuse me of escaping. Please investigate." The judge said that the case was complicated and required further investigation and summoning of witnesses and adjourned the hearing. The defendant was returned to custody.

Hu Nanshan Pharmacy Again Sued for Dispensing Wrong Medicine 143

Ding Jinren, a carpenter from Yancheng residing at 54 Tan Family Residence, Liyuan Road, Shanghai South, suddenly fell ill with typhoid fever in late September. He invited Chinese medicine practitioner Ling Furen to diagnose and prescribe a prescription. He took the prescription to Hu Nanshan Pharmacy at 137 Kangti Road in the French Concession to have it filled. After taking the medicine home and decocting it, his illness worsened. Later, he found out that the original prescription had been changed to a prescription for a woman surnamed Ding to regulate her menstruation. He negotiated with Hu Nanshan Pharmacy but failed to resolve the matter. He then hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court, accusing Hu Zhenxi, the owner of Hu Nanshan Pharmacy, Sun Longshui, an apprentice, and Dr. Ling Furen of negligence in their business and causing injury, requesting an investigation. The owner of Hu Nanshan Pharmacy also accused Ding Jinren's younger brother, Ding Jinrong, and the doctor of colluding in an organized extortion attempt and sued them in the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate. He hired a lawyer to defend against the charges in the Second Special District Court and filed a counterclaim for defamation. Judge Xiong Huicui of the Second Special District Court has held two hearings and summoned Ni Jinren, another doctor who had treated a woman surnamed Ding, to testify. Because the victim Ding Jinren's condition was not stable, he ordered a postponement for another hearing. The Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate investigated the case of Hu Nanshan Pharmacy and others accusing Ding Jinrong, Ling Furen, and others of fraud and decided not to prosecute. The owners of Hu Nanshan Pharmacy and others were dissatisfied with this decision and filed a reason for reconsideration. Now, Ding Wangshi, the woman who mistakenly took Ding Jinren's typhoid fever prescription at the time (29 years old, from Dongtai, husband Ding Chenghua, 38 years old, from Zhenjiang, residing at 100 Dakang Lane, Kangti Road), has now filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court with her husband Ding Chenghua, accusing Hu Xingqing (32 years old, from Yuyao), the junior manager of Hu Nanshan Pharmacy, Sun Longshui, and others of negligence causing injury and requesting a legal investigation. Upon receiving the complaint, Judge Xiong Huicui presided over the hearing in the Second Criminal Court at 4:00 PM yesterday. The plaintiffs, Ding Chenghua and Ding Wangshi, arrived on time, and the defendants, Hu Xingqing and Sun Longshui, also arrived with their defense lawyer, Yu Xiufang. The court first questioned the year and origin of both parties. After the plaintiff briefly stated the purpose of the lawsuit, the court ordered the court to request the investigation file from the local court. Because the file has been sent to the High Court, it has not yet been retrieved, so it was postponed for another hearing. A copy of the counterclaim filed by the defendant was given to the plaintiff in court, and the court was adjourned.

Weather Report 152

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The Shandong region is clear and cold, with gentle southwest to southeast winds. The Yangtze River basin is cloudy and cold, still fine, with strong northwest to northeast breezes. The East China Sea and Taiwan are overcast, with showers. The northeast seasonal wind is becoming stronger. The weather around Northern Luzon is very bad, with a cyclone. As the hurricane is gradually slowing down, it is likely to veer north or northeast. The center of the hurricane at 6:00 AM this morning had moved to within about 60 miles of 17 degrees north latitude and 11.9 degrees east longitude, stopping or moving very slowly. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 58.5 and the lowest was 41.0. On the same day last year, the highest was 61.6 and the lowest was 50.5.

Mourning for the Police Officer Tang Shangjin Who Died in the Line of Duty

Funeral Held This Morning, Police Team Participates in Carrying the Coffin

On the evening of the 5th of this month at 11:50 PM, Police Officer Tang Shangjin, stationed at the Zhongxing Road Police Station in Zhabei, was fatally shot in the chest by robbers while attempting to apprehend them. This was reported in our newspaper. It is now known that after the body was received, the coffin was placed in the open space opposite the scene of the incident. The police station officer, Xie Zhongyi, sent a letter to his hometown in Wuhu, inviting his daughter from his former wife to come to Shanghai. A reply has been received, stating that the daughter is suffering from a leg ailment and is temporarily unable to come to Shanghai. Therefore, the police station has decided to hold the funeral this morning at 9:30 AM, with the coffin temporarily placed at the Yangzhou Public Hall on Pushan Road. The scheduled funeral procedures are recorded below: (A) Funeral Date: November 19th at 9:30 AM. (B) Order of procession for participating teams (using a two-column formation): (1) Public Security Bureau Military Band, (2) Honor Guard, (3) Fire Brigade, (4) Part of the Second Team of the Defense Corps, (5) Students of the Orphanage, (6) First Police Team of this Sub-bureau, (7) Relatives and Friends of the Deceased Officer, (8) Portrait, plus National Music, (9) Hearse, (10) Route of the Funeral Procession: Departing from the sports field of Qingmin Elementary School on Zhongxing Road, via Gonghe Xin Road, Datong Road, Guangfu Road, Huasheng Road, Gonghe Road, Datong Road, Pushan Road, arriving at Yangzhou Public Hall. (C) Notes for Participants: (1) All participants must wear a yellow flower on their left chest, provided by the organizing committee. (2) Each team must have a commander to maintain order during the procession, and please pay attention to avoid disorderly formations. (3) Participants are requested to disperse after reaching the Yangzhou Public Hall. (4) Participants are requested to gather at the Qingmin Elementary School sports field on the west side of Gonghe Xin Road on Zhongxing Road before 9:30 AM this morning. Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, Xinzha Sub-bureau.

Incoming correspondence

Ways of Political Reform (Continued) 155

— Pan Gongzhan

(November, Republic of China Year 24, in Shanghai)

— Respectfully dedicated to the comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Nationalist Party and gentlemen who are interested in discussing political reform —

(A) Regarding the Implementers of the Constitution:

(1) After the draft constitution is passed by the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Nationalist Party, it should be extensively publicized using various methods. At the same time, a deadline should be set to effectively carry out universal public education in each province, city, and county, and to complete local self-government, as preparation for the implementation of constitutional government. The deadline may be determined according to the conditions of each locality, but should be no more than one year. During this period, the central government should strictly supervise. If local officials and senior party officials fail to promote or prepare adequately, they should be severely punished.

(2) Once the draft constitution has been passed by the Fifth National Congress, the date for convening the National Assembly should be set simultaneously, so that the work of preparing for self-government in each locality has a final goal, and at the same time, the people have a reasonable opportunity to participate in politics. The period should also be set within the year of the Republic of China's 26th year.

(3) After the National Assembly passes the Constitution and formally promulgates it, it will naturally be the period for the implementation of constitutional government. However, the provisions of the Constitution, in consideration of certain local circumstances and certain factual limitations, can still separately stipulate the time of effect, and it is not necessary to force all provisions to be implemented nationwide at the same time.

(B) Regarding the Content of the Constitution:

(1) The name of the constitution is the same, but the content of the constitutions of various countries is different. Whether it is a presidential system, a cabinet system, a committee system, a republic, or a monarchy, there can be a constitution. The unwritten constitution of the British style, the written constitution of the American style, and the multi-party alternating system of parliamentary politics are of course examples; the constitutions of Soviet Russia, Italy, and Germany, which adopt a one-party dictatorship system that strengthens administrative power, are also examples. Therefore, we should break the "erroneous notion that whenever a constitution is mentioned, parliamentary politics cannot be avoided," and consider the national conditions ourselves and make a fundamental decision. I believe that our country's constitution should explicitly define "The Republic of China as a Republic of the Three Principles of the People," and at the same time, in spirit, should recognize "The Chinese Nationalist Party as the only party for building a Republic of China based on the Three Principles of the People." Only in this way can the people, to whom sovereignty belongs, enjoy the right to participate in politics on the one hand, and on the other hand, organizations that violate the Three Principles of the People are not allowed to exist. Only then can the existence of the Republic of the Three Principles of the People be guaranteed. Therefore, there should be negative restrictions on the qualifications of citizens of the Republic of China.

(2) The Constitution should be based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy of the Five-Power Constitution, the essence of the "separation of power and ability," to clearly divide the four "political powers" of election, recall, initiative, and referendum, and the five "governing powers" of administration, legislation, judiciary, examination, and supervision. "Governing power" is entirely handed over to the government, and "political power" is controlled by the people (during the transition period, the Nationalist Party leads the people in exercising it). The National Assembly is the organ for exercising "political power," and the central government (including the president and the five yuan) is the organ for exercising "governing power." Therefore, the Legislative Yuan should be recognized as an organization under governing power, and is by no means equivalent to the national assembly in other countries with parliamentary politics. In other words, the Constitution should clearly recognize that the Legislative Yuan is not a supervisory body used to oppose the President or the Executive Yuan, and only the National Assembly has this qualification. (To be continued)

Tidbits 156

— (Baling)

Hating the job you do: This is a common ailment among young professionals, but, young people, we need to think; there are so many unemployed people in society right now, and many college graduates cannot find jobs; having a place where we can earn a living is already a blessing in the eyes of the unemployed; what else do we have to complain about? In my opinion, we should try our best to find interest in our profession and overcome this bad habit of resenting our jobs; we must know that "the other side of the hill looks greener" is human nature, and at the same time, it is our greatest enemy!

Zeng Wenzhenggong said: "If people can take a step back and think, they can be at peace with themselves." I think this sentence is very meaningful. I hope that the young people who generally resent their current jobs will keep this in mind and carefully savor Zeng Wenzhenggong's words. I believe that they will definitely be able to gain infinite benefits and increase their interest in professional life.

Sports Meet Thirty Years Ago 157

— Pastoral Old Man

The evolution of personnel changes follows the trajectory of evolution. Isn’t it ridiculous to look at the past from today's perspective? And the future will also see today in the same way. The establishment of schools in eastern Zhejiang, in the middle of the Guangxu period, Jianhu in Shaoxing, and Chucai in Ningbo, all opened up the national atmosphere. My town is a small county; the establishment of schools was also very early. Regardless of the curriculum at that time, the sports meet held in the entire county is worth mentioning.

The venue was the broad plaza in front of the ×× Temple Hall, where teachers and students from various schools gathered. There was no opening ceremony, no speeches or moments of silence, but the order was well maintained, and there was no noise. There were no events called field events or track events, but there were races. Races were also called walking races, and there were also obstacle races and two-person three-legged races. Jumping included long jump and high jump. It was not called pole vault, but high jump with a pole. There was soccer, but no knowledge of tennis, basketball, or volleyball. There were also arithmetic races, rope skipping, stick jumping, horizontal bar, calisthenics, and blind and mute races, which are not seen today.

What was even more laughable was that after the sports were over, the entire group formed a long snake formation, exited the west gate, and entered the east gate, with everyone singing sports songs, the school flag leading the way, and military music following. The steps were neat, and the atmosphere was high-spirited. Spectators lined the road, and villagers were shocked by the strange event. The so-called military music was one drum and one trumpet, blowing unbearable tunes. Thinking about it today, I can't help but laugh.

Time flies like an arrow. Some of the young athletes in this juvenile sports meet have now emerged as prominent figures. The pastoral old man has achieved nothing, and after visiting the National Games, recalling the past, the scene is still vivid. Sighing that time cannot flow backwards!

Record of a Certain Dancer 158

— Zhuying

Two years ago, my aunt's family employed a maid (commonly known as Big Sister), whose appearance was only average, but she loved to dress up. Because she couldn't stand the poor life in the countryside, she had a falling out with her parents, so all the money she earned was spent on clothes and cosmetics, and not a single cent was sent back.

After living there for half a year, she felt that the money she earned was not enough to spend? So she secretly borrowed money from a shop assistant in a rice store. The shop assistant was quite interested in this maid, so he always granted her requests. Two months later, this secret was discovered by my aunt, so she dismissed her on the pretext. But she rented a house with the shop assistant and lived together.

However, the shop assistant's monthly income was limited, so how could he afford such a wife who spent money lavishly? So then, because his hands and feet were not clean, he was dismissed. At that time, it happened that there were two dancers living together in his house. Chatting idly, they talked about a way out. The maid followed the dancers, learned for a few days, and scraped together a set of clothes, and followed the two dancers into the dance hall.

In the first one or two months, she was only able to provide for the two of them to eat and drink. From the third month onwards, she gradually became popular, and her clothes were changed every three days, every two days. Her husband, the shop assistant from the rice store, although he still stayed at home, guarding the door and cooking, since the end of last year, he also started wearing a suit when he went out. Click-clack, he looked quite impressive. Sometimes children followed behind him, calling him "trailer" and "turtle," but he pretended not to hear.

Because his house is located in the back alley of my aunt's house, I still see her often now. Indeed, she is now a woman who is more modern than anyone else.

Little Western Paradise 160

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-one Tenderly Relying on Others, Over the Courtyard, Pitying the Moon's Appearance, Passionately Instructing the Son-in-law, Listening to the Lion's Roar From the Next Room

Zhiqian smiled and said: Why is Beihai so angry? Beihai walked up to him, still panting a little, shaking his head and saying: Now, I believe that everything in the universe is transferred by matter. If I had political power in my hands, I would first solve the slavery system. The word "slavery" does not only refer to those who are actually working as slaves. There are also those who are not slaves in name, but in fact, they are acting as slaves, and they should also be liberated. Because their suffering as intangible slaves is ten times greater than that of tangible slaves. He spoke like a traveling orator, walking into Cheng Zhiqian's room, and put his schoolbag heavily on the table, making a loud noise. Then he slapped the table with his hand, very hard. He turned his head and said: Humph! Unreasonable! Zhiqian sat on a chair on the side, gently stroking his cheek with his right fingertip, just looking at him and smiling. Only when he stopped speaking did he ask: Beihai, who are you saying is unreasonable? Am I offending you? Beihai then realized and couldn't help but laugh, saying: How dare I say that Mr. Cheng is offending me. But I'm talking about the high-class guests in Little Western Paradise. Mr. Cheng, you are also one of the high-class guests. This, perhaps, is where I am sorry to Mr. Cheng. As he said this, although he still had a lot of bitterness, his face was still red. Zhiqian saw that he was coming from the front, and the level of dissatisfaction with the guests in Little Western Paradise could not exceed that of Jia Duocai, so it was easy to know what he meant. He smiled and said: I understand, is there any new news? Beihai stood in the middle of the room, and said everything he had just seen and heard, with gestures. Naturally, the descriptions were more exaggerated than the actual situation. (363)

Records of Incense and Clouds 161

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The deeper meaning of the Empress Dowager's words did not move me much at first. It was not until now, after experiencing so many years in the course of life, that I realized that her thoughts were indeed very reasonable.

Before noon, she hurriedly issued a very strange and actually meaningless order; she ordered Li Lianying to personally supervise the eunuchs who were in charge of flowers, to chop down the magnolia flower that had suddenly bloomed, break it into pieces, and bury it in the soil; she also strictly ordered them to bury it in a most secluded place, so that no one could step on it, and so that it would not receive any sunlight or rain, so as not to revive it.

After this matter, which she considered most important, was done, her face looked better. Then she said to me:

"A person who bears too heavy a responsibility, it is best to be able to forget his responsibility at any time, otherwise his responsibility will inevitably feel especially heavy, and may even make him weak. Now let us forget our responsibilities! Didn't you say that you can sing Li Bai's 'Qing Ping Diao'? Very good, sing it for me once."

At that time, although her worries had eased a lot, there was still no smile on her face. She only told Li Lianying to quickly call two musicians, one playing the flute and one playing the Xiao, and bring their instruments into the palace to serve. The skills of these two people were very good, and their ensemble was very moving. I also reluctantly put on a smile, raised my voice, and sang Li Bai's Qing Ping Diao; when I was singing, I secretly looked at the Empress Dowager, but saw that the many wrinkles on her face had gradually relaxed, and a more vibrant light had flashed in her eyes. The comfort she needed was actually obtained. I hope she can be quiet from now on.

My Qing Ping Diao was soon finished, and the clear and melodious sounds of the flute and Xiao also dissipated. The two musicians kowtowed and went out.

As these tall palace courtyards were immersed in the dark sky, we were once again shrouded in an atmosphere of serenity, peace, and solemnity! (459) (End of the book)

Record of Chrysanthemum Viewing at Zhenru Temple 162

— Yimei

Walking in the dust of the world, I quite long for a clean environment to wash away my worries. Just then, Mr. Huang Yueyuan, the owner of the Zhenru Huang's Nursery, and my friend, the famous calligrapher Xie Xianou, sent me an invitation. I gladly accepted and ordered a carriage. I arrived at the garden very early, and the guests had not yet gathered. The host told me that the chrysanthemums this year were not as prosperous as in previous years, and that continuous wind and rain had particularly abused the tea. The flowers were already drooping and wilting. If I had come half a month later, there would be no more cold flowers and late blooms to admire. He also said that he had recently met with a certain gentleman and discussed chrysanthemum cultivation methods with him, and there were many experienced talks, such as: "Spring should be refreshing, summer should be moist, autumn should be humid, and winter should be dry. Spring and summer should be lean, strengthening its quality and nourishing its energy; autumn and winter should be fertile, promoting its flowers and cultivating its roots. As for the adjustment of yin and yang, it takes even more effort. Overemphasis on yang is beneficial to flowers and leaves, but not to roots and stems. Overemphasis on yin is beneficial to roots and stems, but not to flowers and leaves. From this, it can be proved that it is appropriate to have yin at the beginning and yang at the end, so that it can be successful." The secrets of chrysanthemum cultivation are all revealed here. Guests came one after another, and then Mr. Huang led us on a tour around. The chrysanthemums were gathered next to the glass flower house. The ten-foot pearl curtain, with its delicate stamens fluttering, hung down to within a foot. The Xueqing lotus flowers were as beautiful as young women. The Lixiang chrysanthemum was like a regular flower, but when held in the hand and smelled, it had the fragrance of pears. It is said that it was a treasure of the inner court, and Empress Dowager Cixi of the Qing Dynasty distributed it to Zhang Xun. Zhang's gardener then privately sold its seeds to others, and thus it became widespread throughout the north and south of the Yangtze River. This small anecdote is quite worth mentioning. Later, the host hosted a banquet for the guests in the bamboo house, pouring grape wine and eating chestnut chicken. The taste was delicious, and we were drunk and full. We said goodbye and left the garden, and with Huang Jiping, Hu Bozhou, Yao Jiguang, Ding Juntao and others, we visited the Canadian Plantation. The ridges and paths were all covered in glass houses, more than ten in total, connected by heating pipes. Entering them, it was as warm as spring. The most abundant plants were tomatoes, with vines rising and bearing fruit, red like frost, which was very pleasing. They ripened twice a year, and the food supply depended on them. Cabbage grows in the north and is cold-resistant and not afraid of frost and snow. It is also placed appropriately to suit its nature. A water suction machine is also set up to draw water from the low-lying areas, so drought is not a concern. Such operations are still an innovation in the country, and I am happy to include them. I deeply hope that they will expand their efforts, so that all kinds of fruits, vegetables, flowers and trees will be bathed in the civilization of science? The future benefits will be ten or a hundred times greater than today, and we can be sure of that.

Places visited

Random Thoughts on Mount Huang (Middle) 163

— Chen Xiaodie

I believe that to tour Mount Huang, the best route is to enter from Bitter Bamboo Creek and exit from Tangkou, so that seeking out scenic spots and exploring secluded places is easier. There are five advantages: From Bitter Bamboo Creek to Lion Forest, the road is flat, and you can go straight up in a sedan chair, which is easier than Tangkou to Manjusri. From Bitter Bamboo Creek, viewing the Nine Dragon Waterfall is advantageous, while from Yungu, viewing the Nine Dragon Waterfall is disadvantageous. Secondly, the beauty of Lion Forest lies in Starting-to-Believe Peak, Scattering Flowers Dock, and West Sea Gate. However, to tour Starting-to-Believe Peak, you must climb Stone Bamboo Shoot Ridge, to tour Scattering Flowers Dock, you must go to Scattering Flowers Convent, and to tour West Sea Gate, you must go to the top of Songlin Ridge. To watch the sunrise, you must go to Bright Top. Without sufficient stamina, you cannot fully enjoy the scenery. Coming from Bitter Bamboo Creek, you arrive at Lion Forest with a smooth journey, without any hardship, your courage is very strong, and you can explore all these secluded and dangerous places. If you come from Manjusri, your stamina is already exhausted and you cannot cope. I asked the only Qing monk, and he knew that those who toured Lion Forest only went to Qin Terrace when climbing Starting-to-Believe Peak, those who toured West Sea Gate did not even know there was Songlin Ridge, and those who toured Scattering Flowers Dock were only three people before me. This is half due to time constraints, but half is also due to stamina limitations. Therefore, coming from Bitter Bamboo Creek is more convenient, thirdly. The bath in Tangchi is unparalleled in the world. Those who come from Tangkou must first take a bath as a pleasure, but after one bath, they rush into the mountains, and after the hardship, their tour is over and they want to bathe in the fairy pool again, which is impossible. Coming from Bitter Bamboo Creek, the bath in Tangchi is the final reward for their mountain tour, so that when they are baptized with nectar, they can look back at the clouds and mountains, and have the obvious pleasure of ascending to heaven. Moreover, the wish to tour the mountain has been fulfilled. If you love this fairy nectar, you may as well linger every day and enjoy the pleasure of undressing, fourthly. The essence of Mount Huang lies in the area from Half Mountain to Lion Forest. Exiting from Yungu inevitably involves a little less touring. Coming from Bitter Bamboo Creek, you enter the scenery step by step, and the scenery becomes better as you advance. By the time your tour is over, there is still the bath in Tangchi to take, transcending the mundane world. Compared to those who exit from Yungu, it makes people feel the sigh of the end of the song and the dispersal of the people, and the green peaks on the river. Therefore, I believe that the entrance to the mountain should really be moved to Taiping, under the scenic spot of Mount Huang, in order to conform to the old site, and the people in Peach Blossom Spring will not be disturbed by the noise of vehicles and horses.

Excellent Academic Performance of New Chinese Boxer Indemnity Students Studying in the UK 166

(Reuters News Agency, London) Mr. Silcock, Director of the Chinese Academic Society, recently returned from inspecting various northern universities and told a Reuters representative that the new Boxer Indemnity students have all settled into their studies smoothly. A total of twenty-four students arrived in the UK in September, including: one studying rayon manufacturing, one studying textile chemistry, one studying wool textiles, two studying aeronautics, two studying naval construction, one studying glass manufacturing, one studying electrical engineering, two studying industrial chemistry, two studying mathematics, two studying animal husbandry, one studying fruit science, one studying human geography, one studying geological geography, one studying tropical pathology, one studying physiology, one studying English, one studying Western history, and one studying law. Among them, fruit science is a new science of grafting fruit trees, which can make fruit trees bear abundant fruit for more than five years. After five years, they no longer bear fruit, but it is also easy to make them bear fruit again. In terms of social life, the students have made many friends. There are about forty students in Manchester. The Anglo-Chinese Association has recently been established, with Sir Stewart as the president and Mr. Mead, a professor of Chinese at the University of Manchester, as the secretary. Mrs. Bryson, who was famous in China, also entertains Chinese students there, and her residence is now a place for these young people to gather and chat. Professor Roxburgh of Liverpool University constantly guides Chinese students to engage in social activities and observe the UK, from which the students benefit greatly. There are fifty Chinese students in Edinburgh, and they have recently established a club in the university district. When Chinese students first arrive in the UK, they often suffer from language problems. According to Mr. Silcock, the English proficiency of this year's group of students is still considerable. He reiterated that Chinese students must improve their English before coming to the UK. Among the students who came to the UK in 1934, there are Mr. Zhang from Beiping and Mr. Zhu from Tianjin, who are studying at Manchester. They are young and eager to learn and have invented a very useful machine. They hope to use it to control the Yellow River flood. Each Boxer Indemnity student is given a fee of £288 per year. Those who enter Oxford or Cambridge University are given an additional £30. According to Mr. Silcock, although this amount is just enough for their needs, it must be spent very carefully, because students have various expenses during holidays, plus clothing and book fees. If they are not thrifty, they will be in financial straits. Mr. Silcock also said that if the China Boxer Indemnity Fund could take this into account and generously increase the allowance, it would be most welcome and certainly necessary, and the custodians can trust that this money will not be misused.

Guangxi Province Implements a Six-Year Plan for Universal Basic National Education 168

The six-year plan for universal basic national education in Guangxi has been approved by the provincial government and is being implemented accordingly. The original text of the outline of this plan is as follows: (A) "Main Points" (1) Relying primarily on political power, supplemented by economic and social forces, to universalize basic national education throughout the province within six years. (2) Using the power of basic national education to assist the following constructions in the province: (a) political construction, (b) economic construction, (c) cultural construction, (d) social construction. (B) "Methods" (1) Guiding aspiring young people throughout the province to return to the fields, shops, and factories, cooperating in learning and labor. (2) Guiding children and adult citizens throughout the province to assist the government in creating a rural construction movement and a national revitalization movement, cooperating in learning, labor, and politics. (C) "Work" Basic national education is divided into children's education and adult education. (1) Children's Education (a) Children aged eight to twelve must receive two academic years of basic national education. (b) Out-of-school children aged thirteen to sixteen must receive one academic year of short-term basic national education. (2) Adult Education (a) Supplemental literacy education. (b) Promoting civil defense training. (c) Perfecting village (street), township (town) organizations. (d) Promoting cooperative movements. The implementation of the aforementioned work takes the National Basic School as the central organization, from which to plan and initiate it. (D) "Teachers" (1) Graduates of normal schools should be employed first, and they should be recruited and trained in stages, with strict performance evaluations. (2) Qualified graduates of the civil defense cadre training brigade should be selected first, and they should be recruited and trained in stages, with strict performance evaluations. (3) Graduates of junior high schools or above, or those who have completed their studies but failed the final examination, should be recruited and trained, and then assigned to different positions, continuing to guide them, with strict performance evaluations. (4) Current elementary school teachers or those who have elementary school teacher qualifications and volunteer to serve should be recruited and trained, and then assigned to different positions, continuing to guide them, with strict performance evaluations. (5) Making efforts to continue to cultivate future teachers who can truly serve basic national education. (E) "Funding" (1) Allocating 20% of the original land tax surcharge for compulsory education in each county. (2) Allocating 30% of the land tax surcharge for education in each county. (3) In the future, after the provincial treasury provides funds for the reorganization of county high schools, all the original county high school funds will be allocated. (4) Allocating other local public assets and funds. (F) "Implementation Procedure" (1) Researching and establishing the Guangxi Institute for Universal Basic National Education. (2) Supervising and guiding, dividing the province into eight guidance zones for universal basic national education based on the current administrative divisions, and establishing National Basic Normal Schools in each zone. (3) Promoting implementation, universally promoting basic national education in all counties of the province within a certain period. (G) "Goals" In addition to the establishment of the Guangxi Institute for Universal Basic National Education (using the results of academic research to assist educational administration in fully popularizing the basic national education plan throughout the province) and the National Basic Education Guidance Zones and National Basic Normal Schools: (1) Before July of the 25th year, National Basic Schools will be universally established in all villages (streets) throughout the province. (2) Before July of the 27th year, Central National Basic Schools will be universally established in all townships (towns) throughout the province. (3) Before July of the 27th year, the one-year short-term basic national education will be completed. (4) Before the 28th year, the two-year basic national education will be completed. (5) Before the 29th year, the preliminary work of village (street) and township (town) construction throughout the province will be completed.

The Asiatic Society Invites Dr. Barger for an Academic Lecture 173

Reporting on the Investigation of Ancient Sites in Peru

Dr. Barger, a British professor at Jiaotong University in this city, was formerly invited by the President of Peru in South America to investigate ancient ruins in that country, study ancient cultures, delve into high mountains of 14,000 feet, and seek the conditions of primitive peoples in Peru. He discovered that these people still existed until the sixteenth century, but were later destroyed by the Spanish, and the remnants no longer exist. The Asiatic Society on Museum Road in this city recently invited Dr. Barger to give a lecture at the Society at 2:30 p.m. on the details of his investigation of ancient sites and the discovery of primitive peoples in Peru, and to show various films taken by Dr. Barger on location to verify the details. Hundreds of Chinese and foreign people attended the lecture, and their interest was very high.

The Municipal Education Bureau Compiles a Report on the Labyrinth Intelligence Test 177

Published in the 8th issue of the Great Shanghai Education Monthly, for Application in Lower Grades of Elementary School and Kindergartens

Intelligence testing is an invention of modern educational science, and its application in education is very extensive. Excellent schools in Western countries invariably use it as the sole tool for admission, grading, and examinations. In the past, our country had various educational standard tests compiled by the Chinese Educational Improvement Society, and there were also revised Binet intelligence tests. However, the procedures were complicated and not very suitable for kindergarten and lower grade elementary school children. In view of this, the Municipal Education Bureau adopted the Labyrinth Intelligence Test materials of Baudette in the United States in the previous year and went to various cities in Jiangsu and Zhejiang to test about 10,000 kindergarten and elementary school children. The materials were statistically organized and compiled into a non-verbal intelligence test suitable for our country. Now, the report is printed as a special issue in the second volume and eighth issue of the Great Shanghai Education Monthly published by the Bureau. The content is divided into seven chapters, listing the implementation of the test, the distribution of results, and the opinions on adaptation. It is said to be a new contribution to educational research in recent days. Subsequently, each primary school and kindergarten intelligence testing, this material is more appropriate, our city each primary school entrance examination or semester end, and may request the Bureau to send people to guide the testing.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (99) 186

— Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"I think you often love to associate with Mr. Ha, and you've thrown Mr. Bei aside," Mrs. Shu said deliberately and slyly.

"Yes, I certainly have; I hate when I can go out and patrol the forest with Mr. Ha, but I have to plow the fields and weed. Mr. Bei thinks that kind of thing is boring and says Mr. Ha is crazy, because he would lie for hours, staring at a fish in the river or a bird in the tree."

"Yes, Mr. Bei is a farmer by nature, and he doesn't know that the work of a naturalist is just as interesting, and maybe just as useful, compared to his own. Don, if you really love these things, I think you really love them, and I like to see this situation, you can have time to study them, and there are also books to help you; but in addition to this, I want you to do one more thing, and to do it tirelessly, otherwise you will regret it later, and feel that you have to start all over again."

"Yes, teacher," Don said docilely, but his face showed that he was inevitably frightened by the seriousness of Mrs. Shu's last few words, because he had no connection with books, but he was clearly determined to study anything she mentioned.

"Do you see that cabinet with twelve drawers?" This was another unexpected question.

Don had indeed seen two tall, old-fashioned cabinets, each standing on one side of the piano; he knew them well, and often saw nails, chestnut paper, and similar useful items taken from the various drawers. He nodded and smiled slightly. Mrs. Shu continued,

"Well, don't you think those drawers are a good place for you to put eggs, pebbles, shells, and moss?"

"Ah, that's great, but you don't want to see my things, as Mr. Bei said, "piled up everywhere," do you?" Don exclaimed, suddenly sitting up, his eyes shining as he looked at the old furniture.

Commercial News

Finance: Rumors of Spot Exports; Gold Market Activity 198

Chips Increase to 20,000; Continuous Rise of 5.6 Yuan Despite Mid-Course Adjustments

Yesterday, the gold market rose due to rumors of 14,000 taels of gold being exported in cash. There was a sudden drop due to external supply midway, but confidence remained strong, and prices stabilized in the end. The market has become more active. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets in both England and the United States were flat. Forward silver prices in Montreal fluctuated. Exchange rates were flat. Spot gold prices in London were unchanged. The Central Bank's listed prices were stable in both England and the United States. Customs gold unit prices were unchanged. The standard gold price remained at 1150 yuan, with little impact. Pre-market trading opened at around 60 yuan. Fuxingyong sold taels at high prices, once dropping to 58 yuan, but Dadecheng and Hengyu bought, and confidence improved. Rumors circulated that a large batch of spot goods would be shipped for export on Saturday, and buying interest in the market was strong, rising to 61.2 yuan. The morning opened high, but demand and supply varied, and the market was uncertain. It was anticipated that the Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) would list prices, and prices in both England and the United States would be flat, leading to fluctuations. Chinese merchants were eager to buy, and Mobil continued to purchase, once rising. However, HSBC took advantage of the high prices to sell, and large players in the market, including Qingfayong, Chunyuan, Yongfuyong, and Taiheng, actively sold, leading to oversupply and a gradual decline, falling below 60 yuan and once becoming weak. Chinese merchants still bought on the cheap, and the domestic market was peaceful and gradually stabilized, rising back above 60 yuan. The late market was stable, and the mainland bought US dollars, leading to strong buying interest and price increases. However, because supply continued to pour in at high prices, it soon became calm again. The first Indian silver report was flat, with little impact. Later, due to many parties selling, it once declined, but did not break the 60-yuan mark. The second Indian silver report was also flat, and the situation fluctuated again. Forward exchange rates tightened and finally strengthened again. Its trend was quite firm, but due to the support of the banking sector, it still could not break away from fluctuations. The swap discount had fallen to within 10 yuan. A record of the day's market situation is as follows:

The opening price in the morning was 1161 yuan, an increase of 4.5 yuan from the previous Saturday. Dadecheng, Qingfayong, and Huihixiang immediately rose from 0.5 jiao to 2.5 yuan. Fuxingyong sold, falling to 1.3 yuan. Hengyu, Huihixiang, Wanfeng, Dadecheng, Yifeng, and Yongshang rose to 2.8 yuan. Yarn and Cotton Manufacturers Said to be Delivering Goods Yarn Prices Fall by One Yuan This Month 203

Distant Months Remain Firm Due to Reduced Yarn Inventory

The yarn market is stable, gradually showing signs of settling down. This is largely due to the calming of rumors about the current situation, and after the local authorities dispelled these rumors, market sentiment has become more peaceful and the market has returned to normal. However, due to the approaching delivery period this month, although buyers are preparing to take delivery, it is said in the market that manufacturers are also delivering goods. Therefore, near-term prices fell in the afternoon, but distant months remained firm due to the reduction in yarn inventory.

Gold Rooster Turns Downward in the Afternoon

At the opening of the standard yarn market, prices for all months were uniformly high. The market price for gold was good, and general unfounded rumors subsided, improving sentiment. There were few new sellers, and the first round of prices for each month rose by 7, 8, or 9 jiao. By the second and third rounds, it was heard that the cotton market was flat and spot yarn transactions were sluggish, resulting in a slight decline. As a result, the price for this month fell by 4 jiao compared to the closing price of the previous day, while distant months rose by 1, 3, 4, or 5 jiao. The market turned softer at the afternoon opening as factories were reportedly delivering goods this month, and bullish speculators at Tongji also emerged, dampening sentiment slightly. However, most major bulls remained unmoved. As a result, the price for this month fell by 6 jiao, while distant months showed mixed gains and losses, ranging from 1, 2, or 3 jiao.
