Yesterday, the Ke Xian rice saw brisk arrivals and sales. The market has an ample stock, and new arrivals keep coming. Rumors are also rampant. The market originally showed signs of leveling off, but the Tianjin merchants suddenly stepped up purchases, and local merchants and hoarders became active again. Therefore, after the opening price in the morning, all grades of higher-quality rice showed a promising trend. However, due to too many rumors in the market and the lack of activity from Ke hoarders, the market leveled off again in the afternoon. A total of 2,000 bags of Gan rice, 360 bags of Yong rice, more than 1,700 bags of Wen-Tai rice, and 250 bags of Fuzhou rice were sold throughout the day. Prices were similar to the previous day. Foreign rice was scarce and prices were firm. Yesterday, there were 200 bags of Siamese rice and 50 bags of No. 3 Saigon rice, with prices gradually increasing.

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, the sources of various merchant groups were even more abundant, with more than 80 arrivals (totaling more than 16,000 shi). The local sales market has been generally flat, and it was even worse yesterday when two rice shops declared liquidation, causing great losses to merchants. Therefore, all merchants are wary, leading to even slower sales. As a result, the price of Hou-Zao and other Japonica rice fell by as much as 3 to 4 jiao. About 3,000 bags of Bao-Wei Thin Rice, from Tianjin, Qingdao, Yantai, etc., were sold, and prices only decreased by 1 to 2 jiao. Beiyang Jian-Huo rice fell by a jiao or so. Yin-Bian rice also decreased by 2 to 3 chi.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, there were more than 60 arrivals from various routes in Hexia. Bai Japonica rice was sluggish and slow to sell, and prices fell by another 2 to 3 jiao. Bao-Wei Thin Rice sold slightly better, and prices decreased by about a jiao. Zao rice sold in small quantities and prices increased by a small jiao or so. Yangbu Jian rice prices were also reduced by 1 to 2 jiao, and Bai Yuan rice also decreased by a small 2 jiao. Du Jian rice was weak, with few inquiries, and other types of rice also decreased by a small jiao or so.

Sesame Opens at Twelve Yuan 211

–––––Donations May Be Exempted

Since foreign merchants opened sesame trading at eleven yuan, the market situation has been firm, prices have been rising steadily. The total number of transactions last week was around 3,800 tons. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson sold at twelve yuan, but there was no response to the telegram. Yuanxing Foreign Company received a reply, so it immediately sold 300 tons at a price of twelve yuan for delivery in December. Therefore, the spot raw sesame market is popular. Yesterday, 2,300 to 2,400 bags of various sesames were opened. Because some felt that the Guangdong Province drama donation delegation had returned to Shanghai and claimed that exemptions could be obtained, factory sales of yellow beans resumed. Yesterday, a total of more than 7,000 bags of various beans were sold, and prices rose by three or four fen. There were also more than 1,400 bags bound for Shantou and Chuzhou. Therefore, the future situation has become stable.

Sugar Market Domestically Produced "Red-Turned" Sugar Plunges by About One Yuan 212

Yesterday, the sugar market trend remained stable. The guild set the price for No. 24 coarse white sugar at 22 yuan and 5 fen. Re-exported goods were priced at 7 yuan, and transactions took place. Zhenji No. 1 fine white sugar from local factories was priced at 21 yuan, a decrease of 1 jiao. Prices for Nos. 2, 3, 4, and 5 remained unchanged. The Sugar Industry Cooperation Company exchanged 2,500 bags of "Five Rams" Cantonese coarse white sugar at 22 yuan and 5 fen, with 1,710 bags being transacted. 1,000 bags of Dutch coarse white sugar for re-export were transacted at 6 yuan and 9 jiao, up 5 fen from last Friday. 1,500 bags of No. 2 Cantonese fine white sugar were priced at 21 yuan and 2 jiao, with only 10 bags being transacted. The remaining Nos. 2 and 4 white sugars were priced at the original price, with no transactions. There were more than 400 bags of "Red-Turned" goods opened by the Chao merchants (named because they were turned red from Chaoshan), priced at 14 yuan and 1 jiao, a sharp drop of about 1 yuan compared to the previous round.

Dried Goods Tianjin Red Dates Rebound by Half a Yuan 214

Tianjin red dates, due to a relatively abundant harvest, had been gradually decreasing in price. Yesterday, it was heard that some merchants were opening prices, which rebounded by four or five jiao compared to before. The trend has tightened and merchants are unwilling to sell at market prices.

Oil Market New Asphalt Oil Is Already Popular 215

New Macheng Oil from Hankou Has Also Arrived

Asphalt oil is currently in the new production season. Because of good harvests everywhere, the production period is earlier than expected. Lan oil from Zhejiang is increasing in production daily. Various presses in the Jiaxing area of western Zhejiang have started pressing Ben Che oil, and new oil has arrived in Shanghai. The first batch of goods is selling for 18 yuan per dan to Shanghai, but there are not many transactions. Because the candle and incense shops in this port are doing very little business, the usage has decreased, so the sales of asphalt oil have not been strong. Moreover, the current situation is difficult and credit is tight, making promotion difficult. However, prices are already low, and it is feared that there is little hope of further price reductions. The market situation in Hankou is also very stable. Chongjing oil is priced at 13 liang, and some merchants are unwilling to sell. A small amount of new Macheng oil has already arrived in Hankou, and Chen oil is also priced at 12 liang and 5 qian. Fortunately, sales are not strong. If the sales market becomes more active, price increases will be inevitable, as the cost for merchants is high. Therefore, they will consider increasing prices as soon as they have a transaction. Local merchants in this port have very thin inventories. The agreed-upon selling price for Chongjing oil is 21 yuan and 2 jiao per dan, and Macheng oil is 19 yuan per dan.

Silk and Tea Qimen Black Tea Still Handled by Merchants 216

Qimen black tea is a famous specialty of our country. It was previously heard that the government, in order to develop foreign trade, intended to bring Qimen tea under the unified trade of state-run cooperative organizations. Subsequently, the Qimen Tea Industry Association and the Shanghai Tea Industry Guild expressed the advantages and disadvantages of the plan and requested the abandonment of the previous proposal. It is now heard that the central government also considers this matter to be a form of competition with the people for profit. In consideration of the business operations of the majority of merchants, the matter will still be handled by merchants.

Steel and Metal Ribbed Steel Bars Continue to Rise 217

40-foot-long ribbed steel bars are seeing large-volume purchases from merchant groups and construction groups. The price is good, as industry colleagues who hold the goods have a firm mentality. The estimated price is 130 yuan per ton, and better-quality steel bars are priced at 135 yuan. It has been found that more than 200 tons of steel bars have been opened for sale in the market in the past two days, but the inventory is low, which has improved sentiment.

Discourse

The Problem of Nearsightedness 218

— By Zhang Ji

A Tokyo dispatch from the 13th: "Recently, the number of nearsighted students in Japan has suddenly increased. Fifty to sixty percent of all students need to wear glasses. The Ministry of Education considers this a major problem in education. The School Building and Equipment Council invited Dr. Nagai, Dean of the Medical Department of Tokyo Imperial University, Professor Oyama of the Engineering Department, Dr. Kamitsu, Chairman of the Illuminating Engineering Institute, Dr. Ito of the Film Promotion Association, and Mr. Iwahara, head of the Physical Education Division of the Ministry of Education, to the Ministry of Education on the 12th. They reported on the results of recent experiments conducted at the university-affiliated schools of the Faculty of Arts and Sciences on the effects of lighting, desk placement, and shape on students' eyesight."

In today's era of advanced optics, nearsightedness is not difficult to correct with lenses. However, it is still a physical defect. Therefore, it is better to prevent it than to try to fix it after the fact. The Japanese Ministry of Education considers the fact that more than half of elementary school students are nearsighted to be a major educational problem and is studying countermeasures. This is of great significance for improving the health of the nation's citizens. Whether or not the nation's citizens are healthy is largely determined during childhood. Nearsightedness, in particular, often develops gradually during childhood due to a lack of attention to eyesight. Therefore, the most effective way to prevent future citizens from developing nearsightedness is to pay attention to elementary school students.

There are no accurate statistics on the number of nearsighted people in our country, but in general, most intellectuals are nearsighted, while fewer people in the working class are nearsighted. In recent decades, school education in our country has gradually developed, but due to practical limitations, little attention has been paid to classroom lighting and students' line of sight from their seats. This has already affected students' eyesight, and the phenomenon of burning the midnight oil under the test system is even more unimaginable. However, the people of our country have not paid attention to this serious problem.

The Japanese Ministry of Education has begun to pay attention to the problem of nearsightedness. I believe that the problem of nearsightedness in our country is even more serious than in Japan and requires appropriate countermeasures. It is also particularly urgent, and I hope that the responsible authorities will not shirk their responsibility and will quickly take steps to improve the situation.

Goddess 219

— Written by Jiang Mi

Northwest of the Kunlun Mountains, at the point where Buzhou Mountain is interrupted, steep cliffs stand upright, facing each other like city prices on the left and right, forming a natural gatehouse. Behind the gatehouse is a sea of water, vast and boundless, connected to the sky. In front of the gatehouse is a flat land, covered with lush green grass and many fallen fruits. The mountain is covered with strange trees, with leaves like jujubes, flowers the color of gold, and calyxes like agate. The flowers are as large as magnolias and have large, peach-shaped fruits. White clouds swirl on the top of the mountain, mingling with the color of the sky. (1)

Storytelling 220

— Hu Weixiong

The days in winter have grown shorter. Confined in their cramped thatched huts, the children are even too listless to play their favorite game of hide-and-seek. When they see the last rays of the sun reflecting from the opposite mountain valley onto the open ground, they immediately raise their small eyes and search the sky for crows returning to their nests. After being cooped up all day, they can now tell their grandmother a lie: "We're going to the bridge to look for Dad." And like a flock of ducklings leaving their coop, they slip away.

The sky is filled with gray clouds. Crows circle the treetops, their calls like the wails of ghosts in the deep mountains, leading the sick to suspect that some misfortune may soon occur. The children run onto the bridge, staring at the setting sun in the opposite mountains, comparing the size of the sun each sees – this is based on a Mid-Autumn Moon story their grandmother told, saying that if the moon appears as large as a bathing tub, it signifies the arrival of a true emperor. So the children will shout that the moon is as big as a cartwheel. Among their companions, in their small wisdom, they search for the most enormous thing they see in their daily lives to boast about being the emperor. Later, they compare the sun to the moon. As long as there's a chance to compare, everyone scrambles to be the emperor.

The sun has completely disappeared into the mountain valley. Only a few streaks of purple-gold light are reflected on the distant clouds, which has almost become a habit. At this time, the intermittent clanging of the bamboo clapper of the old neighbor selling sweet congee floats over from the official road. His carrying pole is reversed, with the congee stove carried behind him. He wears his tattered felt hat pushed back on his forehead, sometimes singing love songs from his youth. Seeing the children at the bridge, he calls out from afar: "Business was good today, all the congee is sold out. I'll save some for you tomorrow." He smiles, turns the corner by the orange grove below the pond, and waves to the children.

Without sweet congee to eat, the children are not disappointed. Having been confined for a day, they're happy to slip away to the bridge, like letting a tethered ox graze freely. They watch the sun, play emperor—they are already quite content. Moreover, after the sweet congee seller returns, they can meet their father. Their father can make all kinds of sugar horses and sugar boats to sell in the city. His carrying pole has a spinning wheel. The section with sugar horses and sugar boats is just a narrow line; it costs one copper coin to spin it once. But those sugar horses and sugar boats are carried in and out every day without ever being spun. Father only makes some odd

Page 16

and ends of sugar pieces to fulfill a large market; these scraps are still left over every day, and the children look forward to them. When Father's carrying pole reaches the bridge, everyone jumps up to grab the sugar pieces to eat. Although Father shouts: "Slow down! Slow down! Go home and divide them," they are snatched up clean before they even get home.

Grandmother hears their noise and also supports herself with a cane to come to the door to see what's happening. "Was business good?" she says to her son, then touches this child's head, that child's head, and says with a smile, "Don't fight, your father is tired!"

Father puts the sugar pole down in the house and takes out his dry tobacco pipe from his waistband to light it and smoke. The children surround the sugar pole, counting the copper coins Father earned today from a cloth bag. Father leans back in his bamboo chair and says to Grandmother: "Today was a general market day; there were many happy events in the city. Good luck, I did a lot of business!"

The children hand the money bag to Grandmother and crowd around Father, clamoring to go to the city to play. Father holds the youngest brother in his arms, and one by one, they all gather around Father's knees. Father touches one's face, smells another's mouth, laughing. Grandmother is busy preparing dinner in the back room. Naturally, the children all swarm to the table again, seeing the same old dishes. The eldest child says:

"Dad did good business, let's eat meat tomorrow!"

Although Grandmother rolls her eyes at him, Father agrees, saying he'll bring meat back tomorrow. Father quickly eats dinner, lights the stove, and prepares to make scraps of sugar. The children surround Grandmother, wanting her to tell a story. This is the daily evening ritual. Grandmother has no fresh stories left, but the children don't believe her. Some grab Grandmother's cane, some climb onto stools to pull at Grandmother's false hair bun. Grandmother gently hits them a few times, and finally begins:

"Once upon a time, there was a family that had a son... and the moon looked as big as a cartwheel... later he became the emperor... that was Emperor Taizu of Ming..."

Before the story is finished, the children, one by one, fall asleep leaning against Grandmother's knees. When Grandmother carries the children to the back room, Father says softly: "Mom, you should sleep too, I'll come when I finish a few sheets of sugar." He raises his head and looks out the window, "Tonight, the moon looks as big as a bathtub, but it's a pity the children are all asleep..."

Song Introduction 221

The Joy of Rural Life

The joy of rural life is without sighs, my humble thatched cottage is all I need. In spring, I raise silkworms to provide clothes, in winter, the surplus is white rice. The joy of rural life is truly unrefined, drunk and singing loudly, patting my belly. Chickens and dogs bustle in front of the door, hemp and mulberry thrive on the ground. Although there is no pearl wine with palm fronds, there is clear wine in abundance. Although there are no pork or mutton delicacies, there are fish and shrimp to satisfy. Although there are no longans or lychees, there are water chestnuts and lotus roots. Although there are no exotic vegetables, there are "wu song" and tender "fei" sprouts. Although there are no singing beauties, there are village girls accompanying me. Rice I grow, wine I make, cotton I spin, coarse cloth I weave. I don't care about petty poverty, I don't care about great wealth. A leaky boat is still passable, half is my own, no need to hire. Just eat meat, don't be vegetarian, yellow-legged chicken, cook in a pot, add some salt, some vinegar, simmer taro, fry tofu, eating slowly until dusk approaches. Bamboo bed, soft straw mattress, just stay overnight until tomorrow, such joy is truly timeless.

Storytelling Ballads 223

Cheng Fangzhou, Li Liansun, Mao Jiashu

Hua Mei (1060) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "The Mistake of Bigamy"

Old husbands and wives nagging. Beside them, a young man sighs. Saying that he doesn't want a despotic marriage. It will lead to strange things in the future. Parents frequently give well-meaning advice. She comes from a famous family, with jade-like beauty. The dowry is plentiful. Everyone says it is a wealthy family. Heaven bestows a good match upon us. You don't need to work to become a groom. How can you say more to stop it. You must agree tonight. Little does he know that the young man has a lover. Living in Shanghai like glue. Hiding it from his family, already married. Now he is burning with anxiety. Later, he reluctantly becomes a groom. Thinking he can get both gold and beauty. A big mistake is planned without awareness. The net of law is tightly drawn. The lover in Shanghai is very suspicious. Rushing to the countryside to ask the truth. Just when the newly married couple is intimately talking. She is filled with anger, burning with rage. She tells the whole story. Blaming the man for being too sly. The young man's newly wedded wife realizes she has been deceived. Immediately, she faints, unable to speak. Later, the two accuse him of bigamy. The iron chains clank as he enters prison. Misfortune brought on by himself is difficult to escape.

Xia Hesheng, Three Smiles

Dun Ben (800) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening: "New Peach Blossom Spring"

Continuous rain, sadness fills the chest. Traveling men worry, hating the sky. I take a volume of opening lyrics, sit on the sofa. Reading carefully until drowsy. Suddenly, my body is on the side of a vast ocean. All around are steep cliffs. I jump into a small boat to be the boatman. Ignoring the wind and waves, rushing forward. Suddenly an island stands before me. I leave the boat and step onto the land, full of fun. Because of the beautiful birds singing joyfully. Towering strange rocks, water gurgling. Trees on both sides are extremely lush. There are also exquisite stone caves, taking the work of heaven. Entering the cave deeper and deeper, traveling a hundred steps to see the sky. Originally, it was a vast plain, a wide road. Moreover, peach blossoms cover the ground, brightly red. Extremely beautiful, like red rain. Swaying in various poses, like crimson clouds. The fragrant wind fills the flower country. Spiritually pleased, heart filled with joy. Chickens and dogs hear each other, rural neighbors connect. Travelers greet each other politely. There are several, graceful and slender young women. Light clothes revealing their chests. Their clothes are unlike those of humans. An old immortal with a child's face and crane's hair comes. Saying that this place is a Peach Blossom Island, a tranquil realm. Children, it is truly a joy to meet you here. We are, people who came here to avoid the chaos of the late Ming and early Qing dynasties. Remotely separated from the mortal world, the road is impassable. Coming to his home to drink fragrant tea. The taste is the same as jade nectar. I ask, the country is in danger. What high plans are there to save the declining situation. The immortal says, the weak are prey to the strong, it has been said since ancient times. Only hold on to perseverance and become heroes. Human power can turn the heavenly numbers around. The theorem of cycles has its end. After a short moment, the light fades. I and him, promise to meet again, hastily say farewell. Winding through the peach blossom spring. The sky is dark, a strong wind rises. The clothes are thin, the body cold. Busily searching for a boat to sail in the sea. Who knows, suddenly a sea monster, long and large. The bloody mouth faces the boat. Heart and gall tremble, oar falls. Ignoring life, closing both eyes. Later, I open my eyes and see nothing. Originally, I was sitting alone in the room. The sound of rain outside the window hasn't stopped. The fragrant tea on the table is still warm. Realizing, the roar of the sea monster was a neighbor's belch. A dream of Nanke. I only hope to visit the place again. To visit the immortals in Peach Blossom Spring. The lingering interest of Liu Lang is even stronger.

Silver Jottings 228

— Zhi'er

I saw a "antique new book—Mother" in the market. Looking closely, I realized that it was a special issue of Tianyi Company's new film "Mother".

The "Mother" special issue has a "Meng Teaching Son" picture in the "antique" yellow floral design.

According to those who have seen the test screening of "Mother", after reading the special issue, there is no need to watch the movie, because "Mother" is a "new" "Meng Mu Teaches Son" - this sentence has a problem, readers should focus on "Meng Mu Teaches Son", the so-called "new" is that she wears a cheongsam and a suit.

It is said that after the publication of the "Mother" special issue, Gao Tianxi made a small fortune. "The thing is this": Tianyi Company originally only planned to collect 200 yuan in advertising fees in the "Special Issue". Mr. Gao had "far-sightedness" and saw that there was a profit to be made in this, so he contracted it. As a result, the advertising fees reached a huge 400 yuan, and Mr. Gao pocketed 200 yuan in one go.

—It is predicted that Tianyi Company will release a "special issue" for each new product in the future. (Editor's note: There is a reason for this, but there is no evidence to check, so just note it and wait for correction.)

Shen Bao Architecture Weekly

Architect Xu Jingzhi Selected for the Architecture of Tan Guoli's Central Museum 229

Construction Cost 1.4 Million Yuan

The preparatory office of the National Central Museum, after selecting the address next to the Zhongshan Gate inside the city, engaged thirteen architects of Chinese nationality through the Construction Committee to participate in the design selection. The Construction Committee also formed a review committee to carry out the review, which was completed earlier. The first choice was architect Xu Jingzhi of Xingye Architectural Firm in this city, who was hired as the architect of the museum. Xu said that most of the architectural designs had been finalized, but there were still some minor architectural details that needed to be modified. Xu recently returned to Shanghai from Beiping to work on modifications under the guidance of Liang Sicheng, an engineering consultant to the Central Museum Construction Committee. Construction may begin within the year. The process of design selection and the detailed architectural plan are recorded below.

Design Selection Process

The architectural design regulations were issued on June 5th of this year, inviting thirteen renowned architects to participate in the project: (1) Li Zongkan of Shanghai, (2) Li Jinpei of Shanghai, (3) Xu Jingzhi of Shanghai, (4) Xi Fuquan of Shanghai, (5) Zhuang Jun of Shanghai, (6) Chen Rongzhi of Guangzhou, (7) Lu Qianshou of Shanghai, (8) Tong Jun of Shanghai, (9) Guo Yuanxi of Tianjin, (10) Dong Dayou of Shanghai, (11) Yu Binglei of Nanjing, (12) Yang Tingbao of Beiping, (13) Su Xiaxuan of Shanghai. All twelve contestants except Su Xiaxuan submitted their designs to the preparatory office of the Central Museum by August 20th, numbered in order using the Heavenly Stems, and handed over to the five review committee members for review. The members were: Zhang Daofan, representative of the Construction Committee; Hang Liwu, representative of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Trustees; architect Liu Minzhen; Li Ji, director of the preparatory office; and Liang Sicheng, specialist committee member and engineering consultant. On September 2nd and 3rd, review committee members Li Ji and Liang Sicheng reviewed each design in detail. The design with the "Ren Jie Di Ling" (Outstanding People and Resourceful Land) seal was disqualified for violating the regulations. Most of the remaining eleven competitive designs exceeded the budget or the area did not meet the requirements. The following points were used to analyze each design:

(1) Overall site layout, (2) Layout of each hall, (3) Relationship between halls, (4) Size of the area, (5) Possibility of future expansion, (6) Vertical traffic between floors, (7) Light distribution, (8) Interior height, (9) Simplicity and ease of structure, (10) Overall three-dimensional layout, (11) Layout of each facade, (12) Detailed programs for each part of the building, (13) Other

Xu Jingzhi Wins First Prize

Among them, items 1, 2, 3, and 5 were especially scrutinized. Using a secret ballot, the "Yi" design was unanimously selected as the winner. The original comments of the review committee are recorded as follows: "In the overall layout, the author was able to overcome the difficult limitations of the irregular "cleaver-shaped" site and master it. The narrow "handle" part connecting to Zhongshan Road was made the main entrance, and the "Yuanmen" was used for the east-west streets to create important gateways, showing that the author had considered the importance of the roads. The front garden is lively and easy to attract visitors. The asymmetrical layout also facilitates the phased construction of the three halls independently. The overall building's consideration of the terrain height is unmatched by other designs and is a special feature of this design. Looking at each hall: the public hall at the entrance is extremely suitable. The hall leads to the exhibition areas of each hall on both sides, and the directors of each hall and the director of the museum are also located in the four corners of this hall, making communication convenient. The working areas of each hall are on the ground floor below the director's office, concentrating the work without interfering with each other. In terms of work, the organization is very flexible. In terms of floor area, only this design can meet the regulations and even exceed them. Most of the exhibition halls are on the same floor, which avoids visitors having to go up and down stairs, which is also a special feature of this design."

"The vertical traffic of the working area of each design is convenient. Most of the exhibition rooms are well-lit except for a small portion, and they are of varying heights, making it easy to accommodate exhibits of different sizes. On the exterior, the three-dimensional interlocking connection of the three halls and the museum's administrative department is very appropriate. The main hall and the exhibition halls of the three halls are in stark contrast and can be harmonized. The offices, exhibition halls, and storage rooms of the three halls are fully expressed on the outside, without the disease of false concealment, which are all features of this design. In each part and component, the author shows a deep understanding of Chinese palace architecture, so it was selected."

The author is architect Xu Jingzhi of Xingye Architectural Firm in this city. Xu is a rising star in the Chinese architectural world in recent years. The Agricultural Experiment Station in the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum in Nanjing and the recently completed Shanghai Fish Market were selected. He is honored to be appointed as the architect of the Central Museum, a huge project worth 1.5 million yuan.

Overall Architectural Plan of the Museum

The total area of the museum in the plan is 275,000 square feet. The museum's general administrative conference room, offices of various sizes, lecture hall, public storage area for the public, sales area for publications, staff dormitory canteen, and worker dormitory, etc., occupy approximately 25,000 square feet. The transportation section occupies 10,000 square feet. The remaining part is the main humanities, natural science, and technology museum, totaling approximately 80,000 square feet. The exhibition halls and equipment of each museum are recorded below:

Humanities Museum

(1) General storage room, (2) Special storage room (security door), (3) Unpacking room (with temporary registration), (4) Stone tool workshop, (5) Bone tool workshop, (6) Metal tool workshop, (7) Pottery workshop, (8) Porcelain workshop, (9) Specimen preparation room, (10) Carpenter's room, (11) Photography room (photography retouching, developing), (12) Disinfection room, (13) Four research rooms (each 15 square feet), (14) Toilet and washroom. The receiving process for newly arrived items in the humanities museum is as follows:

Items are delivered from the outside, (1) Unloaded, (2) Unpacked, (3) Temporarily registered, (4) If necessary, sent to the respective workshop for repair, (5) Officially registered, (6) Sent to the accounting department, (7) Returned to storage or display.

The following exhibition halls: (1) Prehistoric culture exhibition hall, (2) Chinese historical culture exhibition hall (A) Shang and Zhou, (B) Qin, Han, Wei, and Jin dynasties, (C) Southwest ethnic culture exhibition hall, (5) Foreign ethnic group exhibition hall, (6) Systematic and classified exhibition hall, (7) Temporary exhibition hall.

Natural Science Museum

(1) Unpacking room, (2) Mineral and rock room, (3) Paleontology room, (4) Zoology and botany room, (5) Anthropology room, (6) Research room (four or five rooms), (7) Photography room, (8) Drafting room, (9) Worker's room (for two to four people), (10) Washroom. The following exhibition halls: (1) Astronomy and meteorology exhibition hall, (2) Geology and geography exhibition hall, (3) Mineral and rock exhibition hall, (4) Zoology and botany exhibition hall, (5) Anthropology exhibition hall.

Technology Museum

(1) General storage room (for storing models), (2) Special storage room (divided into four or five large rooms, dedicated to storing valuable crafts, such as porcelain, lacquerware, glass, etc.), (3) Unpacking room, (4) Drafting and painting room, (5) Metalworking shop, (6) Foundry and blacksmith shop, (7) Woodworking shop, (8) Plaster, stone, and mud workshop, (9) Configuration and painting workshop, (10) Photography and dark room, (11) Two research rooms, (12) Worker's room (for two people), (13) Washroom and toilet. The following exhibition halls: (1) Chinese famous old industry exhibition hall, (2) Architecture and architectural equipment exhibition hall? (A) Chinese architecture, (B) Western architecture, (C) Urban design, (D) Building materials, (E) Ventilation, heating, cooling, and lighting equipment, (F) Sanitary water supply, (3) Transportation exhibition hall, (1) Ancient transportation models, (2) Modern transportation, (Zi) Roads, (Chou) Land, (Yin) Water, (Mao) Aviation, (4) Mechanical engineering exhibition hall, (1) Thermal engineering, (2) Metalworking manufacturing, (3) Hydraulic power, (4) Boilers must be located in the basement. (5) Textile and other, (6) Agricultural tools, (5) Electrical engineering exhibition hall, (1) Electricity generation and transmission, (2) Electrical communication, (3) Electricity image, (6) Chemical and metallurgical exhibition hall. (1) Metallurgy, (2) Pottery, (3) Acid and alkali, (4) Papermaking, (5) Other, (7) Physics and chemistry exhibition hall, (1) Timepieces, (2) Weights and measures, (3) Physical instruments, (4) Chemical instruments. (8) Printing, photography exhibition hall, (9) Temporary exhibition hall.

Museum Site

Next to Zhongshan Gate inside the city of Nanjing, north of Zhongshan Road, the environment is as shown above. The address covers 100 acres, south of Zhongshan Temple, west of the Central Party Headquarters base, south of the Yizhu School horticultural field, and southeast to Zhongshan Road.

Construction Cost

The total cost is 1.4 million yuan. Excluding the cost of heating, boilers, electric lights, ventilation, fire prevention, and sanitary equipment, which is approximately 300,000 yuan, the net construction budget is 1.1 million yuan, with a 5% range of flexibility at that time.

New Daxia Company Building to Be Completed Soon 230

— Ah Shou

On the Bund, another magnificent new-style building is about to appear. This new building belongs to a large department store company called Daxia, located at the corner of Nanjing and Xizang Roads. The building has nine floors, covering an area of approximately five acres, with an additional three acres for future expansion. The bottom four floors are purely for the company's business and sales, and the remaining five floors are planned to be developed into a recreational and entertainment center.

According to the architects Zhu and Yang who are responsible for the building, no other department store in Shanghai has a larger floor area than this emerging company. Each floor is approximately 4,000 square feet, and there is a basement sufficient for the needs of each sales department. The most attractive features of the new building are: (1) Escalators allow people to ascend as if walking on flat ground, automatically rising and descending; (2) Eight new-style, high-speed elevators are available for passengers; (3) The latest electric freight elevators have also been installed to facilitate the transportation, supply, and distribution of goods; (4) The air circulation throughout the building has also been considered. The ground floor and basement are equipped with hot and cold air conditioning control, so that customers and staff can enter the building as if nothing is happening, even in the heat of summer or the cold of winter; (5) The internal installation parts strive for simplicity and generate ten thousand times the efficiency, so that goods do not take up much space and customers can easily choose.

The fifth floor is planned to be developed into a tea room and restaurant, striving for a grand scale and making the most of the space. As for the other upper floors, the goal is to make them entertainment venues to entertain guests, or to specially open up a cool and refreshing place to escape the summer heat, and to provide Chinese theaters, Chinese and Western cinemas, stages, etc. In short, the upper floors will be made an area for entertainment and enjoyment as much as possible. No expense will be spared to make it magnificent and welcoming, a place where guests will never tire of visiting. The rooftop garden is planned to be arranged in a Chinese style, with pavilions, terraces, towers, temples, and peaks. During the summer, strolling among them, looking out at the racecourse in the distance, Nanjing Road nearby, and admiring the magnificent scenery of birds singing, flowers fragrant, pavilions, and terraces, feeling the cool breeze blowing, one's mind becomes clear and intoxicated in the realm of art, and the summer heat is completely dispelled.

The new building is not yet fully completed and is currently being decorated. Once the interior is arranged and the exterior is improved, a good day will be chosen for the opening. However, the upper-level entertainment venues cannot be arranged and decorated properly for a while, and a few months' delay is decided. Thus, after about a year of construction, a new page in the history of Shanghai architecture, a nine-story grand new building, the Far East New Department Store, is about to appear before our eyes.

Design of Factory Buildings (Part 1) 231

— Bo Ping

In the midst of the call for industrial revitalization in China, although there is an economic downturn, many industries are closely related to national defense and are therefore being gradually built. When we design a factory, we must at least design according to the factory laws stipulated by the central government, taking into account the interests of the factory itself and the safety of the workers. In Shanghai, there are many industrialists and capitalists? Their factory interior designs are so-so, leading to major disasters. The rupture of a boiler can mean the lives of hundreds or thousands of people. This is such a serious problem! A safe factory design is based on the following three principles:

(1) Solid Construction! If the construction is not solid, the vibration of the machinery will cause the walls to tilt.

(2) Sufficient Lighting! Insufficient lighting greatly affects production and has a huge impact on the health of workers.

(3) Appropriate Materials - The selection of building materials is the most important part of factory design. For example, steel-reinforced concrete is the best building for factories. Wooden buildings are not suitable for factories that are prone to explosions.

(1) Site Selection

Site selection is the first problem to be solved in design. In theory, it is determined by supply, manufacturing, and demand. Supply is the problem of raw materials. The factory should be near the raw material production area. This is a fixed axiom, because if it is too far from the raw material production area, it will cost a lot of transportation, which will increase the cost. This is not in line with economic principles. Other things to pay attention to are the problem of power. The so-called power is coal, water, and gasoline. We know that every factory needs these three things. Sometimes, the place we plan to use has raw materials and coal, but the water supply is insufficient or the water composition does not meet the requirements, so we have to change the original plan. Secondly, what is related to site selection is manufacturing. We know that manufacturing uses machinery, but manpower is equally important. If we want a large amount of manpower, we must be in the city. If we want low wages, we must be in the countryside. This depends on the situation and long-term considerations. There are no fixed principles. Demand is sales. The most consumption is in cities. Some things are needed more urgently and more in the countryside than in cities, so the location of our factory is based on the above three principles.

(2) Types of Buildings

The factory-style buildings, in terms of theory, have the following four types, each with its own strengths and weaknesses. There is no fixed standard, and it depends on the nature of the factory. For example, consider the following:
